• I checked the target on 192.168.2.98:4242. It does not look like an STM32F030C8T6.

  What I observed:

  - The ESP32JTAG remote identifies target 1 as STM32F1 L/M density M3.
  - After attach, the core register state is live at PC=0x080000A2.
  - The halted register values include r2=0x40011000 and r12=0x40021000.

  Why that is a mismatch:

  - STM32F030C8T6 is STM32F0, which is a Cortex-M0.
  - The probe is reporting a Cortex-M3 / STM32F1-class target instead.
  - 0x40011000 matches the old STM32F1 GPIO register map, not the STM32F0 GPIO map, which is normally at 0x4800xxxx.

  Conclusion:

  - The connected target is almost certainly not an STM32F030C8T6.
  - It looks much closer to an STM32F1 low/medium-density device, such as an STM32F103C8T6-class board.
  - If the silk really says stm32f030c8t6, then one of these is likely true:
      - the silk/board labeling is wrong
      - the SWD wires are landing on a different board/device
      - the MCU on the board has been replaced or the board variant is not what the silk suggests

  Relevant repo entries:

  - configs/boards/stm32f030c8t6.yaml
  - assets_golden/duts/stm32f030c8t6/manifest.yaml

  If you want, next I can do a tighter identification pass for the actual F1 target and tell you which F1 family it most likely is.

› Sorry, : it should be "I connected PC13 to esp32jtag P0.1" . So PC10 -> ESP32JTAG P0.1. How will do a machine/AI check and confirm? Show me your plan first before doing anything


• Current setup is ambiguous, so I would not touch hardware or firmware yet.

  You wrote both:

  - PC13 -> ESP32JTAG P0.1
  - So PC10 -> ESP32JTAG P0.1

  Those are not the same plan. Since the existing LED is on PC13, this distinction matters.

  Plan once the pin is confirmed:

  1. Confirm the actual jumper

  - If it is PC13 -> P0.1, I can directly machine-check the same net the onboard LED uses.
  - If it is PC10 -> P0.1, I must first patch firmware so PC10 mirrors the LED timing, otherwise that wire does not prove the LED state.

  2. Use the smallest safe validation path

  - Reuse the current stm32f103c6 blinky firmware baseline.
  - Avoid changing unrelated board setup or pack structure.

  3. Choose the check method

  - For PC13 -> P0.1:
      - keep the LED blinky firmware
      - run a signal-observation test on P0.1
      - confirm repeated transitions at the expected faster blink cadence
  - For PC10 -> P0.1:
      - add a temporary mirror output on PC10 synchronized with PC13
      - flash it
      - observe P0.1
      - confirm the mirrored waveform

  4. What counts as machine confirmation

  - AI/tool captures edges on P0.1
  - frequency/duty are consistent with the flashed blink loop
  - this proves the MCU is driving the observed net as expected

  5. What it does and does not prove

  - If PC13 -> P0.1, it strongly confirms the LED net is toggling.
  - It still does not prove the LED package itself is physically emitting light if the LED or resistor were damaged, but it is the correct electrical machine-check for “visible LED blink”.
  - If PC10 -> P0.1, it confirms only the mirrored debug pin unless we deliberately sync it to LED behavior in firmware.

  6. Execution after confirmation

  - inspect the existing board/test profile
  - either reuse it directly or add one temporary observed-signal test
  - flash
  - capture
  - report exact measured result

  Confirm which one is actually connected:

  - PC13 -> P0.1
  - or PC10 -> P0.1

  - Use the ESP32JTAG logic/signal capture path to observe P0.0.
  - Expect a low-frequency square-wave corresponding to the current 2x-faster blink loop.

  4. Define pass criteria

  - Detect repeated high/low transitions on P0.0
  - Confirm frequency is in the expected coarse range for the current delay loop
  - Confirm the signal is stable over the capture window

  5. Interpret the result correctly

  - PASS means the PC13 net is toggling electrically, which is the right machine/AI confirmation for the LED drive signal.
  - It does not prove the LED package itself is physically emitting light if the LED/resistor is damaged, but it does prove the MCU is driving the LED net.

  6. If capture fails

  - First suspect wiring on PC13 -> P0.0
  - Then suspect board-specific LED loading or wrong pin assumption
  - Only after that consider firmware changes

  7. Execution sequence I would use

  - inspect the existing stm32f103c6 board/test definitions
  - run one direct observed-signal test against P0.0
  - if needed, add a tiny temporary test plan that captures sig on P0.0
  - report measured frequency/edges and whether that matches the blink firmware

  If you want me to proceed, I’ll implement or reuse the minimal observed-signal test and run the capture on P0.0.

• Plan for a STM32F103C6T6 golden suite:

  Use the existing STM32F103C8T6 staged suite as the primary template, not STM32F407VET6. F407 has many peripherals that F103C6T6 simply does not have, so “similar” should mean same staged structure and same validation philosophy, not the same test count.

  Target Shape
  I would build this as a new canonical staged suite for the exact DUT, likely:

  - board: stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like
  - pack: packs/stm32f103c6t6_golden.json
  - instrument: ESP32JTAG on 192.168.2.98
  - transport: SWD over gdb_remote, plus ESP32JTAG web LA for GPIO observation

  I would organize it as:

  - Stage 0: board alive
  - Stage 1: internal/self tests
  - Pre-Stage2: connectivity proof
  - Stage 2: functional loopback tests
  - Stage 3: richer proof/banner/signal tests

  What I Can Cover
  For STM32F103C6T6, the realistic full suite should focus on these:

  Stage 0:

  - pc13_blinky_visual
  - minimal_runtime_mailbox
  - pc13_fast_machine_probe or a cleaner equivalent machine proof

  Stage 1:

  - timer_mailbox
  - systick_mailbox
  - internal_temp_mailbox
  - iwdg
  - unique-id / flash-size / reset-cause self checks
  - optional simple flash read/write test if we want an internal NVM check

  Pre-Stage2 connectivity:

  - digital jumper probe 1
  - digital jumper probe 2
  - ADC threshold probe
  - SPI wire-present probe
  - UART TX probe
  - optionally UART RX probe if we add a proper host-to-target injection path

  Stage 2:

  - GPIO loopback
  - EXTI trigger
  - PWM/capture
  - UART loopback
  - UART multibyte
  - UART DMA
  - SPI loopback
  - ADC loopback
  - wiring_verify

  Stage 3:

  - GPIO signature / signal proof
  - banner-style proof tests
  - optional richer timing/banner proofs if they add value

  What I Would Not Claim
  I would not market this as “every feature” in the F407 sense, because F103C6T6 does not have:

  - CAN
  - DAC
  - FPU
  - RNG
  - RTC battery-domain style suite parity with F4/H7 golden families
  - advanced DMA/peripheral breadth comparable to F407
  - large-memory / flash-RW stress value comparable to bigger parts

  I would also probably not include I2C in v1 unless the bench has proper pull-ups and stable wiring. On F103-class bring-up, I2C is often where time gets wasted unless the fixture is explicit.

  Recommended Wiring For The Suite
  Keep current:

  - SWDIO / SWCLK / GND to ESP32JTAG
  - PC13 -> P0.0 for machine-observed LED-net proof
  - onboard LED on PC13

  Add these canonical jumpers:

  - PB0 <-> PB1
    for GPIO loopback / digital connectivity
  - PB8 <-> PB9
    for EXTI and timer-edge / PWM-capture style tests
  - PA0 <-> PA1
    for ADC loopback / analog threshold proof
  - PB15 <-> PB14
    for SPI loopback
  - PA9 <-> PA10
    for UART local loopback

  Optional better UART bench path:

  - PA9 -> external UART RX
  - PA10 <- external UART TX
    This is only needed if you want true host-driven UART tests instead of board-local loopback.

  Optional LA enrichments:

  - PA4 -> P0.0
  - PA5 -> P0.1
    Only if we want richer Stage 3 signature-style tests separate from PC13.

  Concrete Test List I Would Build First
  Version 1 candidate suite:

  - stm32f103c6_pc13_blinky_visual
  - stm32f103c6_minimal_runtime_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_timer_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_systick_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_internal_temp_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_iwdg
  - stm32f103c6_pb0_pb1_probe
  - stm32f103c6_pb8_pb9_probe
  - stm32f103c6_pa0_pa1_adc_probe
  - stm32f103c6_pb15_pb14_probe
  - stm32f103c6_uart_tx_probe
  - stm32f103c6_wiring_verify
  - stm32f103c6_gpio_loopback_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_exti_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_pwm_capture
  - stm32f103c6_uart_loopback_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_uart_multibyte
  - stm32f103c6_uart_dma
  - stm32f103c6_spi_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_adc_mailbox

  That would already be a strong, realistic golden suite for this MCU class.

  Implementation Plan

  1. Formalize the DUT

  - add or upgrade the stm32f103c6t6 DUT manifest to canonical-golden target shape
  - bind it to the .98 ESP32JTAG fixture, not the old .106 one

  2. Lock the canonical bench contract

  - record exact wiring in board/manifest
  - add pre_stage2_connectivity
  - define what is auto-covered vs not auto-covered

  3. Reuse the existing F103C8T6 assets where safe

  - many F103 mailbox tests can be ported with exact C6 linker/startup/memory limits
  - do not blindly reuse C8 memory map assumptions

  4. Build the missing exact-MCU wrappers

  - exact 32 KB flash / 10 KB RAM
  - target-specific linker and startup where needed

  5. Bring up connectivity probes first

  - before Stage 2, prove the jumpers are actually alive
  - fail fast on wiring faults

  6. Add Stage 2 functional tests

  - only after the connectivity layer is stable

  7. Add Stage 3 proof tests

  - signal/banner proofs after the functional layer works

  8. Live validation

  - first per-test
  - then full pack
  - then closeout + reusable skill capture

  Expected Outcome
  I would aim for:

  - a clean stm32f103c6t6_golden canonical pack
  - around 18 to 22 tests
  - stronger than the current minimal baseline
  - smaller and more realistic than stm32f407vet6_golden
  - aligned in structure with the newer STM32 golden families

  If you want, next I can turn this plan into the exact proposed pack contents and the exact wiring table you should build on the bench.

  └ firmware/targets/stm32f103c6/ael_mailbox.h (+49 -0)
     1 +#ifndef AEL_MAILBOX_H
     2 +#define AEL_MAILBOX_H
     3 +
     4 +#include <stdint.h>
     5 +
     6 +/*
     7 + * AEL Debug Mailbox — STM32F103C6T6
     8 + *
     9 + * SRAM: 10 KB (0x20000000-0x200027FF)
    10 + * Mailbox at 0x20002400 (1 KB below SRAM end).
    11 + */
    12 +
    13 +#define AEL_MAILBOX_MAGIC    0xAE100001u
    14 +#ifndef AEL_MAILBOX_ADDR
    15 +#define AEL_MAILBOX_ADDR     0x20002400u
    16 +#endif
    17 +
    18 +#define AEL_STATUS_EMPTY     0u
    19 +#define AEL_STATUS_RUNNING   1u
    20 +#define AEL_STATUS_PASS      2u
    21 +#define AEL_STATUS_FAIL      3u
    22 +
    23 +typedef struct {
    24 +    uint32_t magic;
    25 +    uint32_t status;
    26 +    uint32_t error_code;
    27 +    uint32_t detail0;
    28 +} ael_mailbox_t;
    29 +
    30 +#define AEL_MAILBOX  ((volatile ael_mailbox_t *)AEL_MAILBOX_ADDR)
    31 +
    32 +static inline void ael_mailbox_init(void) {
    33 +    AEL_MAILBOX->magic      = AEL_MAILBOX_MAGIC;
    34 +    AEL_MAILBOX->error_code = 0u;
    35 +    AEL_MAILBOX->detail0    = 0u;
    36 +    AEL_MAILBOX->status     = AEL_STATUS_RUNNING;
    37 +}
    38 +
    39 +static inline void ael_mailbox_pass(void) {
    40 +    AEL_MAILBOX->status = AEL_STATUS_PASS;
    41 +}
    42 +
    43 +static inline void ael_mailbox_fail(uint32_t error_code, uint32_t detail) {
    44 +    AEL_MAILBOX->error_code = error_code;
    45 +    AEL_MAILBOX->detail0    = detail;
    46 +    AEL_MAILBOX->status     = AEL_STATUS_FAIL;
    47 +}
    48 +
    49 +#endif /* AEL_MAILBOX_H */

• The official-pattern difference is small but concrete: ST-style SPI2 setup enables AFIO together with GPIOB and SPI2, while our bare-metal SPI2 path only enabled GPIOB and SPI2. I’m applying that exact delta first before I spend time on more speculative SPI changes.

• Edited firmware/targets/stm32f103c6_spi_loopback/main.c (+2 -2)

      1 +# STM32F103C6T6 Golden Suite Closeout
      2 +
      3 +**Date:** 2026-04-01
      4 +**Board:** `stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like`
      5 +**Pack:** `packs/stm32f103c6t6_golden.json`
      6 +**Instrument:** `esp32jtag_stm32_golden` @ `192.168.2.98:4242`
      7 +**Status:** final canonical full-pack rerun completed `18/18 PASS`
      8 +
      9 +## Summary
     10 +
     11 +`STM32F103C6T6` is now formalized as a canonical staged golden suite on the
     12 +ESP32JTAG STM32 bench. The final live proof is the repo-native pack run:
     13 +
     14 +```bash
     15 +PYTHONPATH=. python3 -m ael pack --pack packs/stm32f103c6t6_golden.json --board stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like --stop-on-fail
     16 +```
     17 +
     18 +The suite now covers Stage 0 board-life checks, Stage 1 internal/self tests,
     19 +pre-Stage2 connectivity proof, and Stage 2 functional loopback/timing/UART
     20 +tests on real hardware.
     21 +
     22 +## Canonical Bench Contract
     23 +
     24 +- SWD: `P3`
     25 +- reset: `NC`
     26 +- verify view: `P0.0`
     27 +- `PC13 -> P0.0`
     28 +- `PC13 -> LED`

     31 +- `PA0 <-> PA1`

     33 +- `PA9 <-> PA10`
     34 +- common ground to probe ground
     35 +

     47 +- `runs/2026-04-01_11-17-21_stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like_stm32f103c6_capture_mailbox`

     52 +

     54 +- `runs/2026-04-01_10-57-37_stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like_stm32f103c6_pwm_capture`

     57 +- `runs/2026-04-01_10-58-32_stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like_stm32f103c6_uart_dma`
     58 +
     59 +## What Was Validated
     60 +
     61 +Validated on real hardware in the final canonical rerun:
     62 +
     63 +- `stm32f103c6_pc13_blinky_visual`
     64 +- `stm32f103c6_minimal_runtime_mailbox`
     65 +- `stm32f103c6_timer_mailbox`
     66 +- `stm32f103c6_systick_mailbox`
     67 +- `stm32f103c6_internal_temp_mailbox`
     68 +- `stm32f103c6_iwdg`
     69 +- `stm32f103c6_pb0_pb1_probe`
     70 +- `stm32f103c6_pb8_pb9_probe`
     71 +- `stm32f103c6_pa0_pa1_adc_probe`
     72 +- `stm32f103c6_pb15_pb14_probe`
     73 +- `stm32f103c6_gpio_loopback`
     74 +- `stm32f103c6_exti_trigger`
     75 +- `stm32f103c6_adc_loopback`
     76 +- `stm32f103c6_capture_mailbox`
     77 +- `stm32f103c6_pwm_capture`
     78 +- `stm32f103c6_uart_loopback_mailbox`
     79 +- `stm32f103c6_uart_multibyte`
     80 +- `stm32f103c6_uart_dma`
     81 +
     82 +## Key Repair Findings
     83 +
     84 +1. Exact density matters.
     85 +
     86 +The first SPI loopback attempt was modeled like a larger F103 part and used the
     87 +`PB13/PB14/PB15` SPI2 pin family. That is invalid for `STM32F103C6T6`, which
     88 +exposes only one SPI. The canonical suite therefore defers SPI until the bench
     89 +adds a real `SPI1` loopback path on `PA5/PA6/PA7`.
     90 +
     91 +Reference used during the bounded repair step:
     92 +
     93 +- ST official product page: `STM32F103C6` shows `1 x SPI`
     94 +
     95 +2. Copied startup code must include the real interrupt vectors.
     96 +
     97 +The initial copied `C6` startup only exposed a tiny vector table. Interrupt-
     98 +driven tests such as timer and SysTick did not become reliable until the shared
     99 +`stm32f103c6` startup was fixed to include the needed vectors.
    100 +
    101 +3. Pre-Stage2 connectivity is worth keeping.
    102 +
    103 +The dedicated probe layer for `PB0/PB1`, `PB8/PB9`, `PA0/PA1`, and `PB15/PB14`
    104 +made the Stage 2 loopback and timing failures much easier to classify as
    105 +wiring-vs-firmware instead of guessing from richer tests.
    106 +
    107 +## Deferred Coverage
    108 +
    109 +Not in the canonical suite yet:
    110 +
    111 +- SPI loopback on `SPI1` because the current bench contract does not expose the
    112 +  required `PA5/PA6/PA7` jumper path
    113 +- any host-external UART proof beyond the board-local `PA9 <-> PA10` loopback
    114 +
    115 +This is an intentional scope boundary, not a silent failure.
    116 +
    117 +## Process Note
    118 +
    119 +This work would have been incomplete if it stopped at the code and first pass
    120 +of live validation. The reusable outcome here depends on both:
    121 +
    122 +- a closeout report tying the suite to real run ids
    123 +- a reusable skill capturing the exact density and bench-contract rules
    124 +
    125 +That is why the suite is only considered complete after this closeout and the
    126 +matching skill capture landed.
    127 +
    128 +## Closeout Decision
    129 +
    130 +This round is a valid golden-suite closeout for `STM32F103C6T6`.
    131 +
    132 +The correct conclusion is:
    133 +
    134 +- canonical pack: complete
    135 +- live validation: complete
    136 +- final canonical full-pack rerun: `18/18 PASS`
    137 +- DUT manifest verified state: promoted
    138 +- reusable skill capture: completed

  └ docs/skills/stm32f103c6t6_esp32jtag_golden_suite_skill_2026-04-01.md (+85 -0)
     1 +# STM32F103C6T6 ESP32JTAG Golden Suite Skill
     2 +
     3 +## Use When
     4 +
     5 +Use this skill when building or repairing the `STM32F103C6T6` staged suite on
     6 +the ESP32JTAG STM32 bench at `192.168.2.98:4242`.
     7 +
     8 +Fixture shape:
     9 +
    10 +- SWD on `P3`
    11 +- `PC13 -> P0.0`
    12 +- `PC13 -> LED`
    13 +- `PB0 <-> PB1`
    14 +- `PB8 <-> PB9`
    15 +- `PA0 <-> PA1`
    16 +- `PB15 <-> PB14`
    17 +- `PA9 <-> PA10`
    18 +
    19 +## Core Rules
    20 +
    21 +1. Treat this as exact `STM32F103C6T6`, not generic `STM32F103`.
    22 +
    23 +   `C6` density boundaries matter for both memory layout and peripheral count.
    24 +
    25 +2. Do not assume `SPI2`.
    26 +
    27 +   `STM32F103C6T6` exposes only one SPI. If the bench loopback is on
    28 +   `PB13/PB14/PB15`, that is not a valid canonical SPI path for this MCU.
    29 +
    30 +3. If copied `C6` tests depend on interrupts, verify the startup vectors first.
    31 +
    32 +   A truncated vector table will break timer, SysTick, and EXTI tests in ways
    33 +   that look like firmware logic bugs.
    34 +
    35 +4. Keep `pre_stage2_connectivity`.
    36 +
    37 +   Run the dedicated jumper probes before trusting the richer Stage 2 tests:
    38 +
    39 +   - `PB0/PB1`
    40 +   - `PB8/PB9`
    41 +   - `PA0/PA1`
    42 +   - `PB15/PB14`
    43 +
    44 +5. Reuse the canonical net roles.
    45 +
    46 +   - `PB0/PB1`: simple GPIO loopback
    47 +   - `PB8/PB9`: capture and PWM timing
    48 +   - `PA0/PA1`: ADC loopback and EXTI
    49 +   - `PA9/PA10`: UART loopback
    50 +   - `PC13/P0.0`: LED-net observation only
    51 +
    52 +## Working Validation Shape
    53 +
    54 +Canonical full-pack entrypoint:
    55 +
    56 +```bash
    57 +PYTHONPATH=. python3 -m ael pack --pack packs/stm32f103c6t6_golden.json --board stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like --stop-on-fail
    58 +```
    59 +
    60 +Canonical validated pack:
    61 +
    62 +- `packs/stm32f103c6t6_golden.json`
    63 +
    64 +Representative all-pass pack run:
    65 +
    66 +- `pack_runs/2026-04-01_11-11-47_stm32f103c6t6_golden_stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like`
    67 +
    68 +## Troubleshooting Order
    69 +
    70 +1. Confirm the target family over SWD.
    71 +2. Confirm the exact density before reusing another F103 test.
    72 +3. Run Stage 0 and Stage 1 first.
    73 +4. Run the pre-Stage2 connectivity probes.
    74 +5. Only then trust Stage 2 timing, ADC, or UART failures as real firmware
    75 +   issues.
    76 +6. If a test exceeds the bounded repair window, compare it against official ST
    77 +   docs/examples before spending more time on local guesses.
    78 +
    79 +## Lessons To Keep
    80 +
    81 +- `STM32F103C6T6` is close to `C8T6`, but not interchangeable.
    82 +- A clean staged suite is smaller and more honest than claiming unsupported
    83 +  peripherals.
    84 +- New-pack work is not finished at code plus first pass; it finishes at code,
    85 +  live evidence, closeout, and reusable skill capture.

› What do we have finished? What test do we already have? Do you think we need a more tests ? Do you think every feature of this MCU has been covered? What is missing?


• What is finished:

  The STM32F103C6T6 now has a real canonical golden suite on your .98 ESP32JTAG bench, with live validation complete at 18/18 PASS.

  Main artifacts:

  - pack: packs/stm32f103c6t6_golden.json
  - DUT: assets_golden/duts/stm32f103c6t6/manifest.yaml
  - closeout: docs/reports/stm32f103c6t6_golden_suite_closeout_2026-04-01.md
  - skill: docs/skills/stm32f103c6t6_esp32jtag_golden_suite_skill_2026-04-01.md

  What tests already exist:

  - stm32f103c6_pc13_blinky_visual
  - stm32f103c6_minimal_runtime_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_timer_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_systick_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_internal_temp_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_iwdg
  - stm32f103c6_pb0_pb1_probe
  - stm32f103c6_pb8_pb9_probe
  - stm32f103c6_pa0_pa1_adc_probe
  - stm32f103c6_pb15_pb14_probe
  - stm32f103c6_gpio_loopback
  - stm32f103c6_exti_trigger
  - stm32f103c6_adc_loopback
  - stm32f103c6_capture_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_pwm_capture
  - stm32f103c6_uart_loopback_mailbox
  - stm32f103c6_uart_multibyte
  - stm32f103c6_uart_dma

  Do we need more tests?

  Yes, if the goal is broader MCU coverage rather than a practical golden suite. The current suite is strong for this bench and this MCU class, but it is not “every feature.”

  What is covered well:

  - board alive / flash / runtime
  - timer and SysTick
  - watchdog
  - internal temp ADC path
  - GPIO loopback
  - EXTI
  - ADC external loopback
  - timer capture / PWM measurement
  - UART loopback, multibyte, DMA
  - bench connectivity proof before Stage 2

  What is not fully covered:

  - SPI
    Missing from canonical suite because this MCU only has SPI1, and the bench does not currently provide PA5/PA6/PA7 loopback wiring.
  - I2C
    No I2C tests yet.
  - RTC / backup-domain behavior
    Not covered.
  - low-power modes
    Not covered.
  - DMA beyond UART
    Only UART DMA is covered.
  - flash erase/write endurance-style or option-byte style checks
    Not covered.
  - reset-cause / RCC / clock-tree validation beyond what current firmware implicitly uses
    Not covered as dedicated tests.
  - input channels beyond the current ADC loopback path
    Only one simple ADC path is covered.
  - external interrupt matrix breadth
    Only one EXTI path is covered.
  - timer breadth
    We cover useful timer behavior, not every timer mode/channel.

  Has every feature of the MCU been covered?

  No.

  This is now a credible, useful, live-proven golden suite for the current bench. It is not exhaustive MCU-feature certification.

  What I think is the best next expansion order:

  1. Add real SPI1 coverage

  - requires bench wiring for PA5/PA6/PA7

  2. Add I2C

  - requires explicit pull-ups and a stable loopback/fixture plan

  3. Add reset-cause / flash-size / unique-ID / RCC self-tests

  - cheap to add, high value

  4. Add low-power / wakeup tests

  - only if the bench can observe wake behavior reliably

  5. Add broader ADC and timer-channel coverage

  - useful if you want closer-to-datasheet coverage

  So the short answer is:

  - finished: yes, the canonical STM32F103C6T6 golden suite is complete for the current bench
  - current tests: 18 live-validated tests
  - more tests needed: yes, if you want broader peripheral coverage
  - every feature covered: no
  - biggest missing items: SPI1, I2C, low-power, RTC/backup-domain, broader DMA/clock/reset/flash checks

  └ firmware/targets/stm32f103c6_reset_cause_mailbox/main.c (+38 -0)
     1 +#include <stdint.h>
     2 +
     3 +#define AEL_MAILBOX_ADDR 0x20002400u
     4 +#include "../stm32f103c6/ael_mailbox.h"
     5 +
     6 +#define RCC_BASE        0x40021000u
     7 +#define RCC_CSR         (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x24u))
     8 +
     9 +#define RCC_CSR_RMVF    (1u << 24)
    10 +#define RESET_FLAGS_MASK (0xFC000000u)
    11 +
    12 +#define ERR_NO_FLAGS    0x41u
    13 +#define ERR_CLEAR_FAIL  0x42u
    14 +
    15 +int main(void) {
    16 +    uint32_t before;
    17 +    uint32_t after;
    18 +
    19 +    ael_mailbox_init();
    20 +
    21 +    before = RCC_CSR & RESET_FLAGS_MASK;
    22 +    if (before == 0u) {
    23 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_NO_FLAGS, RCC_CSR);
    24 +        while (1) {}
    25 +    }
    26 +
    27 +    RCC_CSR |= RCC_CSR_RMVF;
    28 +    after = RCC_CSR & RESET_FLAGS_MASK;
    29 +    if (after != 0u) {
    30 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_CLEAR_FAIL, after);
    31 +        while (1) {}
    32 +    }
    33 +
    34 +    AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = before;
    35 +    ael_mailbox_pass();
    36 +
    37 +    while (1) {}
    38 +}

  └ firmware/targets/stm32f103c6_system_identity_mailbox/main.c (+66 -0)
     1 +#include <stdint.h>
     2 +
     3 +#define AEL_MAILBOX_ADDR 0x20002400u
     4 +#include "../stm32f103c6/ael_mailbox.h"
     5 +
     6 +#define SCB_CPUID       (*(volatile uint32_t *)0xE000ED00u)
     7 +#define DBGMCU_IDCODE   (*(volatile uint32_t *)0xE0042000u)
     8 +#define FLASH_SIZE_KB   (*(volatile uint16_t *)0x1FFFF7E0u)
     9 +#define UID_W0          (*(volatile uint32_t *)0x1FFFF7E8u)
    10 +#define UID_W1          (*(volatile uint32_t *)0x1FFFF7ECu)
    11 +#define UID_W2          (*(volatile uint32_t *)0x1FFFF7F0u)
    12 +
    13 +#define RCC_BASE        0x40021000u
    14 +#define RCC_CR          (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x00u))
    15 +#define RCC_CFGR        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x04u))
    16 +
    17 +#define ERR_CPUID       0x31u
    18 +#define ERR_DEVID       0x32u
    19 +#define ERR_FLASH       0x33u
    20 +#define ERR_UID         0x34u
    21 +#define ERR_CLOCK       0x35u
    22 +
    23 +int main(void) {
    24 +    uint32_t cpuid = SCB_CPUID;
    25 +    uint32_t idcode = DBGMCU_IDCODE;
    26 +    uint32_t dev_id = idcode & 0x0FFFu;
    27 +    uint32_t flash_kb = FLASH_SIZE_KB;
    28 +    uint32_t uid0 = UID_W0;
    29 +    uint32_t uid1 = UID_W1;
    30 +    uint32_t uid2 = UID_W2;
    31 +    uint32_t uid_mix = uid0 ^ uid1 ^ uid2;
    32 +    uint32_t hsi_ready = (RCC_CR >> 1u) & 1u;
    33 +    uint32_t sws = (RCC_CFGR >> 2u) & 0x3u;
    34 +
    35 +    ael_mailbox_init();
    36 +
    37 +    if (cpuid != 0x411FC231u) {
    38 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_CPUID, cpuid);
    39 +        while (1) {}
    40 +    }
    41 +
    42 +    if (dev_id != 0x410u) {
    43 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_DEVID, idcode);
    44 +        while (1) {}
    45 +    }
    46 +
    47 +    if (flash_kb < 32u || flash_kb > 128u) {
    48 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_FLASH, flash_kb);
    49 +        while (1) {}
    50 +    }
    51 +
    52 +    if (uid_mix == 0u) {
    53 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_UID, uid0 | uid1 | uid2);
    54 +        while (1) {}
    55 +    }
    56 +
    57 +    if (hsi_ready == 0u || sws > 0x2u) {
    58 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_CLOCK, (hsi_ready << 16u) | sws);
    59 +        while (1) {}
    60 +    }
    61 +
    62 +    AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = (flash_kb << 16u) | dev_id;
    63 +    ael_mailbox_pass();
    64 +
    65 +    while (1) {}
    66 +}

     6 +#define SYST_CSR (*(volatile uint32_t *)0xE000E010u)
     7 +#define SYST_RVR (*(volatile uint32_t *)0xE000E014u)
     8 +#define SYST_CVR (*(volatile uint32_t *)0xE000E018u)
     9 +#define SCB_SCR  (*(volatile uint32_t *)0xE000ED10u)
    10 +
    11 +#define SYST_CSR_ENABLE    (1u << 0)
    12 +#define SYST_CSR_TICKINT   (1u << 1)
    13 +#define SYST_CSR_CLKSOURCE (1u << 2)
    14 +#define SCB_SCR_SLEEPDEEP  (1u << 2)
    15 +
    16 +static volatile uint32_t g_ticks = 0u;
    17 +static volatile uint32_t g_wakeups = 0u;
    18 +static volatile uint32_t g_passed = 0u;
    19 +
    20 +void SysTick_Handler(void)
    21 +{
    22 +    g_ticks++;
    23 +}
    24 +
    25 +int main(void)
    26 +{
    27 +    ael_mailbox_init();
    28 +
    29 +    SCB_SCR &= ~SCB_SCR_SLEEPDEEP;
    30 +    SYST_RVR = 7999u;
    31 +    SYST_CVR = 0u;

    33 +
    34 +    while (1) {
    35 +        __asm__ volatile ("wfi");

    40 +            ael_mailbox_fail(0x51u, (g_ticks << 16u) | (g_wakeups & 0xFFFFu));
    41 +            while (1) {}
    42 +        }
    43 +
    44 +        if (g_wakeups >= 50u && g_passed == 0u) {
    45 +            ael_mailbox_pass();
    46 +            g_passed = 1u;
    47 +        }
    48 +    }
    49 +}

     10 +#define ADC1_SR         (*(volatile uint32_t *)(ADC1_BASE + 0x00u))
     11 +#define ADC1_CR1        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(ADC1_BASE + 0x04u))

     13 +#define ADC1_SMPR1      (*(volatile uint32_t *)(ADC1_BASE + 0x0Cu))
     14 +#define ADC1_SQR1       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(ADC1_BASE + 0x2Cu))
     15 +#define ADC1_SQR3       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(ADC1_BASE + 0x34u))
     16 +#define ADC1_DR         (*(volatile uint32_t *)(ADC1_BASE + 0x4Cu))
     17 +
     18 +#define RCC_ADC1EN             (1u << 9)
     19 +#define ADC_CR2_ADON           (1u << 0)
     20 +#define ADC_CR2_CAL            (1u << 2)
     21 +#define ADC_CR2_RSTCAL         (1u << 3)
     22 +#define ADC_CR2_EXTTRIG        (1u << 20)
     23 +#define ADC_CR2_SWSTART        (1u << 22)
     24 +#define ADC_CR2_TSVREFE        (1u << 23)
     25 +#define ADC_CR2_EXTSEL_SWSTART (0x7u << 17)
     26 +#define ADC_SR_EOC             (1u << 1)
     27 +
     28 +#define ERR_ADC_TIMEOUT 0x61u
     29 +#define ERR_SAMPLE_LOW  0x62u
     30 +#define ERR_SAMPLE_HIGH 0x63u
     31 +
     32 +static void delay_cycles(volatile uint32_t cycles)
     33 +{
     34 +    while (cycles-- > 0u) {
     35 +        __asm__ volatile ("nop");
     36 +    }
     37 +}
     38 +
     39 +static void adc1_init_internal(uint32_t channel)
     40 +{
     41 +    RCC_APB2ENR |= RCC_ADC1EN;
     42 +    (void)RCC_APB2ENR;
     43 +
     44 +    ADC1_CR1 = 0u;
     45 +    ADC1_SQR1 = 0u;
     46 +    ADC1_SQR3 = channel;
     47 +    ADC1_SMPR1 &= ~(0x7u << 21u);
     48 +    ADC1_SMPR1 |=  (0x7u << 21u);
     49 +
     50 +    ADC1_CR2 = ADC_CR2_ADON | ADC_CR2_TSVREFE;
     51 +    delay_cycles(10000u);
     52 +    ADC1_CR2 |= ADC_CR2_RSTCAL;
     53 +    while ((ADC1_CR2 & ADC_CR2_RSTCAL) != 0u) {}
     54 +    ADC1_CR2 |= ADC_CR2_CAL;
     55 +    while ((ADC1_CR2 & ADC_CR2_CAL) != 0u) {}
     56 +    delay_cycles(200000u);
     57 +}
     58 +
     59 +static uint8_t adc1_read(uint16_t *value_out)
     60 +{
     61 +    uint32_t timeout = 500000u;
     62 +
     63 +    ADC1_SR = 0u;
     64 +    ADC1_CR2 &= ~(0x7u << 17u);
     65 +    ADC1_CR2 |= ADC_CR2_EXTSEL_SWSTART;
     66 +    ADC1_CR2 |= ADC_CR2_ADON;
     67 +    ADC1_CR2 |= ADC_CR2_EXTTRIG | ADC_CR2_SWSTART;
     68 +    while (((ADC1_SR & ADC_SR_EOC) == 0u) && timeout-- > 0u) {}
     69 +    if ((ADC1_SR & ADC_SR_EOC) == 0u) {
     70 +        return 0u;
     71 +    }
     72 +
     73 +    *value_out = (uint16_t)(ADC1_DR & 0xFFFFu);
     74 +    return 1u;
     75 +}
     76 +
     77 +int main(void)
     78 +{
     79 +    uint32_t sum = 0u;
     80 +
     81 +    ael_mailbox_init();
     82 +    adc1_init_internal(17u);
     83 +
     84 +    for (uint32_t i = 0u; i < 8u; ++i) {
     85 +        uint16_t sample = 0u;
     86 +        if (adc1_read(&sample) == 0u) {
     87 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_ADC_TIMEOUT, i);
     88 +            while (1) {}
     89 +        }
     90 +        sum += sample;
     91 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = sample;
     92 +        delay_cycles(50000u);
     93 +    }
     94 +
     95 +    {
     96 +        uint16_t avg = (uint16_t)(sum / 8u);
     97 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = avg;
     98 +        if (avg < 1000u) {
     99 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_SAMPLE_LOW, avg);
    100 +            while (1) {}
    101 +        }
    102 +        if (avg > 2200u) {
    103 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_SAMPLE_HIGH, avg);
    104 +            while (1) {}
    105 +        }
    106 +    }
    107 +
    108 +    ael_mailbox_pass();
    109 +    while (1) {
    110 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 ^= 0x00010000u;
    111 +        delay_cycles(200000u);
    112 +    }
    113 +}

      6 +#define RCC_BASE        0x40021000u
      7 +#define RCC_APB2ENR     (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x18u))
      8 +#define RCC_APB1ENR     (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x1Cu))
      9 +
     10 +#define GPIOB_BASE      0x40010C00u
     11 +#define GPIOB_CRH       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOB_BASE + 0x04u))
     12 +#define GPIOB_IDR       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOB_BASE + 0x08u))
     13 +#define GPIOB_ODR       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOB_BASE + 0x0Cu))
     14 +
     15 +#define TIM2_BASE       0x40000000u
     16 +#define TIM2_CR1        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x00u))
     17 +#define TIM2_PSC        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x28u))
     18 +#define TIM2_ARR        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x2Cu))
     19 +#define TIM2_CNT        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x24u))
     20 +#define TIM2_EGR        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM2_BASE + 0x14u))
     21 +
     22 +#define TIM4_BASE       0x40000800u
     23 +#define TIM4_CR1        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM4_BASE + 0x00u))
     24 +#define TIM4_EGR        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM4_BASE + 0x14u))
     25 +#define TIM4_CCMR2      (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM4_BASE + 0x1Cu))
     26 +#define TIM4_CCER       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM4_BASE + 0x20u))
     27 +#define TIM4_PSC        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM4_BASE + 0x28u))
     28 +#define TIM4_ARR        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM4_BASE + 0x2Cu))
     29 +#define TIM4_CCR3       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM4_BASE + 0x3Cu))
     30 +
     31 +#define TIM_CR1_CEN     (1u << 0)
     32 +#define TIM_CR1_ARPE    (1u << 7)
     33 +
     34 +#define ERR_SYNC_TIMEOUT  0x71u
     35 +#define ERR_EDGE_TIMEOUT  0x72u
     36 +#define ERR_PERIOD_RANGE  0x73u
     37 +#define ERR_DUTY_RANGE    0x74u
     38 +
     39 +static uint32_t read_pb9(void)
     40 +{
     41 +    return (GPIOB_IDR >> 9) & 1u;
     42 +}
     43 +
     44 +static void delay_us(uint32_t us)
     45 +{
     46 +    uint32_t start = TIM2_CNT;
     47 +    while ((uint32_t)(TIM2_CNT - start) < us) {}
     48 +}
     49 +
     50 +static uint32_t wait_for_level(uint32_t level, uint32_t timeout_us)
     51 +{
     52 +    while (timeout_us--) {
     53 +        if (read_pb9() == level) {
     54 +            return 1u;
     55 +        }
     56 +        delay_us(1u);
     57 +    }
     58 +    return 0u;
     59 +}
     60 +
     61 +int main(void)
     62 +{
     63 +    RCC_APB2ENR |= (1u << 3);
     64 +    RCC_APB1ENR |= (1u << 0) | (1u << 2);
     65 +
     66 +    /*
     67 +     * PB8: TIM4_CH3 output AF push-pull 50MHz -> CRH[3:0] = 0xB
     68 +     * PB9: input pull-down                    -> CRH[7:4] = 0x8, ODR9 = 0
     69 +     */
     70 +    GPIOB_CRH &= ~0xFFu;
     71 +    GPIOB_CRH |=  0x8Bu;
     72 +    GPIOB_ODR &= ~((1u << 9) | (1u << 8));
     73 +
     74 +    TIM2_PSC = 7u;
     75 +    TIM2_ARR = 0xFFFFFFFFu;
     76 +    TIM2_EGR = 1u;
     77 +    TIM2_CNT = 0u;
     78 +    TIM2_CR1 = TIM_CR1_CEN;
     79 +
     80 +    /* TIM4 at 1MHz: 1ms period, 25% duty on CH3/PB8 */
     81 +    TIM4_PSC = 7u;
     82 +    TIM4_ARR = 999u;
     83 +    TIM4_CCR3 = 250u;
     84 +    TIM4_CCMR2 = (6u << 4u) | (1u << 3u);
     85 +    TIM4_CCER = (1u << 8u);
     86 +    TIM4_EGR = 1u;
     87 +    TIM4_CR1 = TIM_CR1_ARPE | TIM_CR1_CEN;
     88 +
     89 +    ael_mailbox_init();
     90 +
     91 +    if (!wait_for_level(0u, 5000u)) {
     92 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_SYNC_TIMEOUT, 0u);
     93 +        while (1) {}
     94 +    }
     95 +
     96 +    uint32_t rise1 = 0u;
     97 +    uint32_t fall1 = 0u;
     98 +    uint32_t rise2 = 0u;
     99 +    uint32_t last_state = 0u;
    100 +
    101 +    for (uint32_t polls = 0u; polls < 20000u; ++polls) {
    102 +        uint32_t state = read_pb9();
    103 +        if (state == 1u && last_state == 0u) {
    104 +            if (rise1 == 0u) {
    105 +                rise1 = TIM2_CNT;
    106 +            } else if (fall1 != 0u) {
    107 +                rise2 = TIM2_CNT;
    108 +                break;
    109 +            }
    110 +        }
    111 +        if (state == 0u && last_state == 1u && rise1 != 0u && fall1 == 0u) {
    112 +            fall1 = TIM2_CNT;
    113 +        }
    114 +        last_state = state;
    115 +    }
    116 +
    117 +    if (rise1 == 0u || fall1 == 0u || rise2 == 0u) {
    118 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_EDGE_TIMEOUT, 0u);
    119 +        while (1) {}
    120 +    }
    121 +
    122 +    {
    123 +        uint32_t high_us = fall1 - rise1;
    124 +        uint32_t period_us = rise2 - rise1;
    125 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = (period_us << 16u) | (high_us & 0xFFFFu);
    126 +
    127 +        if (period_us < 900u || period_us > 1100u) {
    128 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_PERIOD_RANGE, period_us);
    129 +            while (1) {}
    130 +        }
    131 +        if (high_us < 150u || high_us > 350u) {
    132 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_DUTY_RANGE, high_us);
    133 +            while (1) {}
    134 +        }
    135 +    }
    136 +
    137 +    ael_mailbox_pass();
    138 +    while (1) {
    139 +        delay_us(1000u);
    140 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0++;
    141 +    }
    142 +}

• The failure is now explained by the official ST part description: low-density STM32F103C6 does not give me the broader timer set I assumed, so a TIM4/PB8 test is the wrong target on this MCU. I’m setting that aside and switching the hardware timer-channel test to
  TIM3_CH3 on the existing PB0 -> PB1 loopback instead.

     28 +#define TIM3_ARR        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM3_BASE + 0x2Cu))
     29 +#define TIM3_CCR3       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(TIM3_BASE + 0x3Cu))
     30 +
     31 +#define TIM_CR1_CEN     (1u << 0)
     32 +#define TIM_CR1_ARPE    (1u << 7)
     33 +
     34 +#define ERR_SYNC_TIMEOUT  0x71u
     35 +#define ERR_EDGE_TIMEOUT  0x72u
     36 +#define ERR_PERIOD_RANGE  0x73u
     37 +#define ERR_DUTY_RANGE    0x74u
     38 +
     39 +static uint32_t read_pb1(void)
     40 +{
     41 +    return (GPIOB_IDR >> 1) & 1u;
     42 +}
     43 +
     44 +static void delay_us(uint32_t us)
     45 +{
     46 +    uint32_t start = TIM2_CNT;
     47 +    while ((uint32_t)(TIM2_CNT - start) < us) {}
     48 +}
     49 +
     50 +static uint32_t wait_for_level(uint32_t level, uint32_t timeout_us)
     51 +{
     52 +    while (timeout_us--) {
     53 +        if (read_pb1() == level) {
     54 +            return 1u;
     55 +        }
     56 +        delay_us(1u);
     57 +    }
     58 +    return 0u;
     59 +}
     60 +
     61 +int main(void)
     62 +{
     63 +    RCC_APB2ENR |= (1u << 3);
     64 +    RCC_APB1ENR |= (1u << 0) | (1u << 1);
     65 +
     66 +    /*
     67 +     * PB0: TIM3_CH3 output AF push-pull 50MHz -> CRL[3:0] = 0xB
     68 +     * PB1: input pull-down                    -> CRL[7:4] = 0x8, ODR1 = 0
     69 +     */
     70 +    GPIOB_CRL &= ~0xFFu;
     71 +    GPIOB_CRL |=  0x8Bu;
     72 +    GPIOB_ODR &= ~((1u << 1) | (1u << 0));
     73 +
     74 +    TIM2_PSC = 7u;
     75 +    TIM2_ARR = 0xFFFFFFFFu;
     76 +    TIM2_EGR = 1u;
     77 +    TIM2_CNT = 0u;
     78 +    TIM2_CR1 = TIM_CR1_CEN;
     79 +
     80 +    /* TIM3 at 1MHz: 1ms period, 25% duty on CH3/PB0 */
     81 +    TIM3_PSC = 7u;
     82 +    TIM3_ARR = 999u;
     83 +    TIM3_CCR3 = 250u;
     84 +    TIM3_CCMR2 = (6u << 4u) | (1u << 3u);
     85 +    TIM3_CCER = (1u << 8u);
     86 +    TIM3_EGR = 1u;
     87 +    TIM3_CR1 = TIM_CR1_ARPE | TIM_CR1_CEN;
     88 +
     89 +    ael_mailbox_init();
     90 +
     91 +    if (!wait_for_level(0u, 5000u)) {
     92 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_SYNC_TIMEOUT, 0u);
     93 +        while (1) {}
     94 +    }
     95 +
     96 +    uint32_t rise1 = 0u;
     97 +    uint32_t fall1 = 0u;
     98 +    uint32_t rise2 = 0u;
     99 +    uint32_t last_state = 0u;
    100 +    uint32_t window_start = TIM2_CNT;
    101 +
    102 +    while ((uint32_t)(TIM2_CNT - window_start) < 10000u) {
    103 +        uint32_t state = read_pb1();
    104 +        if (state == 1u && last_state == 0u) {
    105 +            if (rise1 == 0u) {
    106 +                rise1 = TIM2_CNT;
    107 +            } else if (fall1 != 0u) {
    108 +                rise2 = TIM2_CNT;
    109 +                break;
    110 +            }
    111 +        }
    112 +        if (state == 0u && last_state == 1u && rise1 != 0u && fall1 == 0u) {
    113 +            fall1 = TIM2_CNT;
    114 +        }
    115 +        last_state = state;
    116 +        delay_us(1u);
    117 +    }
    118 +
    119 +    if (rise1 == 0u || fall1 == 0u || rise2 == 0u) {
    120 +        ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_EDGE_TIMEOUT, 0u);
    121 +        while (1) {}
    122 +    }
    123 +
    124 +    {
    125 +        uint32_t high_us = fall1 - rise1;
    126 +        uint32_t period_us = rise2 - rise1;
    127 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = (period_us << 16u) | (high_us & 0xFFFFu);
    128 +
    129 +        if (period_us < 900u || period_us > 1100u) {
    130 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_PERIOD_RANGE, period_us);
    131 +            while (1) {}
    132 +        }
    133 +        if (high_us < 150u || high_us > 350u) {
    134 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_DUTY_RANGE, high_us);
    135 +            while (1) {}
    136 +        }
    137 +    }
    138 +
    139 +    ael_mailbox_pass();
    140 +    while (1) {
    141 +        delay_us(1000u);
    142 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0++;
    143 +    }
    144 +}

  - skill: docs/skills/stm32f103c6t6_esp32jtag_golden_suite_skill_2026-04-01.md

  Important findings:

  - live identity on this board is low-density DBGMCU_IDCODE low bits = 0x412
  - that is why the first broader timer attempt around TIM4 was wrong for this MCU; the valid hardware timer expansion is TIM3_CH3 -> PB0, measured through PB0 <-> PB1
  - final all-pass pack evidence: pack_runs/2026-04-01_12-20-18_stm32f103c6t6_golden_stm32f103c6t6_bluepill_like/pack_result.json

  SPI1 and I2C status:

  - both were evaluated and explicitly deferred, not ignored
  - SPI1 needs a valid partner path on PA5/PA6/PA7 or remapped PB3/PB4/PB5
  - I2C needs a real slave/partner path on PB6/PB7 or remapped PB8/PB9
  - the current bench does not provide those, so there is no honest way to claim hardware coverage yet

  Official reference used for the remap/pin constraints:

  - ST RM0008: https://www.st.com/resource/de/reference_manual/cd00171190.pdf

  Current unrelated worktree noise left untouched:

  - ael/civilization/data/run_index.json
  - experiments/esp32jtag/verify_blink.py


› I saw this during your working process : "The failure is now explained by the official ST part description: low-density STM32F103C6 does not give me the broader timer set I assumed, so a TIM4/PB8 test is the wrong target on this MCU. I’m setting that aside and
  switching the hardware timer-channel test to
    TIM3_CH3 on the existing PB0 -> PB1 loopback instead.       "
  What the issue is? How did you fix it?
  Is there any other similar issue fixed? Details of how.
  Are those "how I fixed issues" skills/experence recorded into CE ?


• The timer issue was a wrong MCU-class assumption.

  I first tried to broaden timer coverage with a TIM4/PB8 hardware PWM test. That made sense for larger STM32F103 parts, but your live board identifies as low-density STM32F103C6T6 with DBGMCU_IDCODE low bits = 0x412. On this class, the broader timer/pin choice I
  assumed was not the right target. The failure mode was a mailbox edge-timeout because the expected hardware PWM path never became valid. I fixed it by throwing away that test and replacing it with a hardware-timer test that matches the real MCU and existing bench
  wiring: TIM3_CH3 on PB0, observed through the existing PB0 <-> PB1 loopback. That final test is tests/plans/stm32f103c6_tim3_pwm_pb0_pb1_mailbox.json with firmware in firmware/targets/stm32f103c6_tim3_pwm_pb0_pb1_mailbox/main.c. The wrong test was removed before
  commit.

  There were a few other similar fixes. The biggest one was SPI: I initially followed an F103 pattern that used SPI2-style pins, but STM32F103C6T6 only has SPI1. That meant the attempted PB13/PB14/PB15 path was invalid for this MCU, so I removed that path from the
  canonical suite and documented SPI1 as deferred until the bench has a real partner path. Another real fix was the shared C6 startup code: the copied startup file had a truncated vector table, which broke interrupt-driven tests like timer and SysTick in a way that
  looked like firmware logic bugs. I fixed that in the shared base firmware/targets/stm32f103c6/startup_stm32f103.c, and that is what made the interrupt-based tests stable. A smaller but important process fix was stopping concurrent runs on the same target; when I
  accidentally overlapped a full-pack rerun with a direct test run, I discarded that pack as non-authoritative and reran cleanly.

  Yes, the knowledge was recorded, but in two different ways. First, the repo-level reusable knowledge is explicitly written down in docs/skills/stm32f103c6t6_esp32jtag_golden_suite_skill_2026-04-01.md and the closeout docs/reports/
  stm32f103c6t6_golden_suite_closeout_2026-04-01.md. Second, Civilization Engine auto-recorded per-run outcomes and some automatic “first successful run” skill reflections during execution. What I did not do was manually fill the CE template with explicit
  ExperienceAPI.add(...) entries for each lesson, so the durable human-readable capture is definitely in docs, while CE also has automatic run/skill traces from the session.


› For SPI and I2C tests, they are still not implemented, correct? What wiring is needed for these two?


• Correct. They are not implemented into the canonical STM32F103C6T6 suite yet.

  Why:

  - SPI1 and I2C are deferred because the current bench does not provide a valid partner path for them.
  - I did not want to fake coverage with an invalid topology.

  SPI1 wiring needed

  STM32F103C6T6 only has SPI1.

  Default SPI1 pins:

  - PA5 = SCK
  - PA6 = MISO
  - PA7 = MOSI
  - optional PA4 = NSS

  For a minimal loopback-style proof on one MCU, the practical wiring is:

  - PA7 -> PA6
  - optional PA5 -> ESP32JTAG input if you want to observe clock separately
  - GND -> probe GND

  That is enough for a simple transmit/receive self-check where the MCU shifts data out on MOSI and reads it back on MISO.

  Alternative remapped SPI1 path, if you use remap:

  - PB3 = SCK
  - PB4 = MISO
  - PB5 = MOSI

  Then the equivalent loopback is:

  - PB5 -> PB4

  I2C wiring needed

  I2C is different: a same-peripheral “wire TX to RX” trick is not enough. You need a real bus partner.

  Default I2C1 pins:

  - PB6 = SCL
  - PB7 = SDA

  Minimum workable options:

  1. External I2C slave device

  - PB6 -> slave SCL
  - PB7 <-> slave SDA
  - 3.3V
  - GND
  - pull-ups on SCL and SDA to 3.3V
    Typical: 4.7k to 10k

  2. Second MCU or second I2C endpoint

  - one endpoint provides the slave
  - same shared bus:
      - PB6 shared SCL
      - PB7 shared SDA
      - pull-ups required
      - common GND

  Important:

  - I2C needs pull-ups
  - simple PB6 -> PB7 on the same MCU is not a valid I2C test
  - current bench has no second I2C endpoint and no defined external slave path, which is why I deferred it

  What I recommend

  For easiest next expansion:

  - SPI1:
      - add PA7 -> PA6
  - I2C1:
      - add an external slave on PB6/PB7
      - add 4.7k pull-ups on both lines

  If you want, next I can give you an exact wiring table for your bench and then implement SPI1 first.


› added  PA7 -> PA6 and add PA5 -> P0.1 of esp32JTAG. Skip I2C test. Do spi and still follow the 15min---check doc---10min rule


• You added the right SPI jumper set for a valid SPI1 loopback path. I’m implementing a C6-exact SPI1 mailbox test on PA5/PA6/PA7, validating it live, and I’ll only fall back to ST docs/examples if it burns through the 15-minute window.

      6 +#define RCC_BASE        0x40021000u
      7 +#define RCC_APB2ENR     (*(volatile uint32_t *)(RCC_BASE + 0x18u))
      8 +
      9 +#define GPIOA_BASE      0x40010800u
     10 +#define GPIOA_CRL       (*(volatile uint32_t *)(GPIOA_BASE + 0x00u))
     11 +
     12 +#define SPI1_BASE       0x40013000u
     13 +#define SPI1_CR1        (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SPI1_BASE + 0x00u))
     14 +#define SPI1_SR         (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SPI1_BASE + 0x08u))
     15 +#define SPI1_DR         (*(volatile uint32_t *)(SPI1_BASE + 0x0Cu))
     16 +
     17 +#define RCC_IOPAEN      (1u << 2)
     18 +#define RCC_SPI1EN      (1u << 12)
     19 +
     20 +#define SPI_CR1_CPHA      (1u << 0)
     21 +#define SPI_CR1_CPOL      (1u << 1)
     22 +#define SPI_CR1_MSTR      (1u << 2)
     23 +#define SPI_CR1_BR_DIV16  (0x3u << 3)
     24 +#define SPI_CR1_SPE       (1u << 6)
     25 +#define SPI_CR1_LSBFIRST  (1u << 7)
     26 +#define SPI_CR1_SSI       (1u << 8)
     27 +#define SPI_CR1_SSM       (1u << 9)
     28 +
     29 +#define SPI_SR_RXNE       (1u << 0)
     30 +#define SPI_SR_TXE        (1u << 1)
     31 +#define SPI_SR_BSY        (1u << 7)
     32 +
     33 +#define ERR_TIMEOUT       0x81u
     34 +#define ERR_MISMATCH      0x82u
     35 +
     36 +static void delay_cycles(volatile uint32_t n)
     37 +{
     38 +    while (n-- > 0u) {
     39 +        __asm__ volatile ("nop");
     40 +    }
     41 +}
     42 +
     43 +static void spi1_init(void)
     44 +{
     45 +    /*
     46 +     * PA5 SCK  = AF push-pull 50MHz -> 0xB
     47 +     * PA6 MISO = input floating     -> 0x4
     48 +     * PA7 MOSI = AF push-pull 50MHz -> 0xB
     49 +     */
     50 +    GPIOA_CRL &= ~(0xFFFu << 20u);
     51 +    GPIOA_CRL |=  (0xB4Bu << 20u);
     52 +
     53 +    SPI1_CR1 = SPI_CR1_MSTR | SPI_CR1_BR_DIV16 | SPI_CR1_SSI | SPI_CR1_SSM;
     54 +    SPI1_CR1 |= SPI_CR1_SPE;
     55 +}
     56 +
     57 +static uint8_t spi1_transfer(uint8_t tx, uint8_t *rx)
     58 +{
     59 +    uint32_t timeout = 100000u;
     60 +
     61 +    while ((SPI1_SR & SPI_SR_RXNE) != 0u) {
     62 +        (void)SPI1_DR;
     63 +    }
     64 +
     65 +    while (((SPI1_SR & SPI_SR_TXE) == 0u) && timeout-- > 0u) {}
     66 +    if ((SPI1_SR & SPI_SR_TXE) == 0u) {
     67 +        return 0u;
     68 +    }
     69 +
     70 +    SPI1_DR = tx;
     71 +
     72 +    timeout = 100000u;
     73 +    while (((SPI1_SR & SPI_SR_RXNE) == 0u) && timeout-- > 0u) {}
     74 +    if ((SPI1_SR & SPI_SR_RXNE) == 0u) {
     75 +        return 0u;
     76 +    }
     77 +
     78 +    *rx = (uint8_t)(SPI1_DR & 0xFFu);
     79 +
     80 +    timeout = 100000u;
     81 +    while (((SPI1_SR & SPI_SR_BSY) != 0u) && timeout-- > 0u) {}
     82 +    return 1u;
     83 +}
     84 +
     85 +int main(void)
     86 +{
     87 +    static const uint8_t patterns[] = {0x55u, 0xA5u, 0x3Cu, 0xC3u, 0x96u, 0x69u};
     88 +
     89 +    RCC_APB2ENR |= (RCC_IOPAEN | RCC_SPI1EN);
     90 +    (void)RCC_APB2ENR;
     91 +
     92 +    spi1_init();
     93 +    ael_mailbox_init();
     94 +
     95 +    for (uint32_t i = 0u; i < (sizeof(patterns) / sizeof(patterns[0])); ++i) {
     96 +        uint8_t rx = 0u;
     97 +        uint8_t tx = patterns[i];
     98 +
     99 +        if (!spi1_transfer(tx, &rx)) {
    100 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_TIMEOUT, i);
    101 +            while (1) {}
    102 +        }
    103 +        if (rx != tx) {
    104 +            ael_mailbox_fail(ERR_MISMATCH, ((uint32_t)tx << 8u) | rx);
    105 +            while (1) {}
    106 +        }
    107 +
    108 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0 = ((uint32_t)i << 16u) | rx;
    109 +        delay_cycles(12000u);
    110 +    }
    111 +
    112 +    ael_mailbox_pass();
    113 +    while (1) {
    114 +        AEL_MAILBOX->detail0++;
    115 +        delay_cycles(40000u);
    116 +    }
    117 +}

› What do you thin should be hte next?


• Next best step is I2C, but only after you add a real bus partner.

  Right now the suite is strong for this MCU and bench:

  - 24/24 PASS
  - SPI is now covered
  - the biggest real gap is still I2C

  What I recommend next, in order:

  1. Add a proper I2C1 fixture

  - PB6 = SCL
  - PB7 = SDA
  - common GND
  - pull-ups on both lines, typically 4.7k to 3.3V
  - either:
      - a small external I2C slave device, or
      - a second MCU / controllable I2C endpoint

  2. Then implement an I2C staged path

  - pre-stage2 bus-alive check
  - simple address probe / ACK proof
  - register read/write mailbox test

  3. After that, only if you want broader-than-practical coverage

  - low-power wake variants beyond current WFI
  - more ADC channel coverage
  - more timer channel permutations
  - flash write/erase self-test
  - external UART host-path test instead of only local loopback

  If you want the highest payoff immediately, do I2C. If you want the least hardware work, do flash read/write and broader reset/clock self-checks next.
